   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of countries by intentional homicide rate</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Wikipedia list article
      </div> 
      <p>The <b>list of countries by UNODC homicide rate</b> is typically expressed in units of deaths per 100,000 individuals per year; thus, a mortality rate of 30 (out of 100,000) in a population of 100,000 would mean 30 deaths per year in that entire population, or 0.03% out of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-UNODC_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNODC-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNODC2013_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNODC2013-2">[note 1]</a></sup> The reliability of underlying national <a href="/wiki/Murder#Epidemiology" title="Murder">murder rate</a> data may vary.<sup id="cite_ref-richards-1999-056-p29_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richards-1999-056-p29-3">[2]</a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">UNODC</a> data is used in the main table below.<sup id="cite_ref-UNODC_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNODC-1">[1]</a></sup> In some cases it is not as up to date as other sources. See farther down as to why its data is used over other sources. </p>
      <p>Research suggests that intentional homicide demographics are affected by changes in trauma care, leading to changed lethality of violent assaults, so the intentional homicide rate may not necessarily indicate the overall level of societal violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris_2002_128–166_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris_2002_128–166-4">[3]</a></sup> They may also be under-reported for political reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2018)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>A study undertaken by the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Declaration_on_Armed_Violence_and_Development" title="Geneva Declaration on Armed Violence and Development">Geneva Declaration on Armed Violence and Development</a> estimated that there were approximately 490,000 intentional homicides in 2004. The study estimated that the global rate was 7.6 intentional homicides per 100,000 inhabitants for 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">UNODC</a> (United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime) reported a global average intentional homicide rate of 6.2 per 100,000 population for 2012 (in their report titled "Global Study on Homicide 2013").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC201412_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC201412-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNODCXLS_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNODCXLS-9">[8]</a></sup> UNODC calculated a rate of 6.9 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">
       <input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png/440px-UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png/660px-UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png/880px-UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png 2x" data-file-width="1069" data-file-height="281"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:UNODC_definition_of_homicide.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>The class of violent deaths documented in this article is intentional killing of others outside of war. Deaths occurring during situations of civil unrest are a grey area.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <p>Intentional homicide is defined by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a> (UNODC) in its <i>Global Study on Homicide</i> report<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC201410_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC201410-11">[10]</a></sup> thus: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>Within the broad range of violent deaths, the core element of intentional homicide is the complete liability of the direct perpetrator, which thus excludes killings directly related to war or conflicts, self-inflicted death (suicide), killings due to legal interventions or justifiable killings (such as self-defence), and those deaths caused when the perpetrator was reckless or negligent but did not intend to take a human life (non-intentional homicide). </p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>Though some discrepancies exist in how specific categories of intentional killings are classified, the definitions used by countries to record data are generally close to the UNODC definition, making the homicide rates highly comparable at the international level.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014102–103_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014102–103-12">[11]</a></sup> UNODC uses the homicide rate as a proxy for overall violence, as this type of crime is one of the most accurately reported and internationally comparable indicators.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Figures from the Global Study on Homicide are based on the UNODC Homicide Statistics dataset, which is derived from the criminal justice or public health systems of a variety of countries and territories.<sup id="cite_ref-executivesummary_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-executivesummary-14">[13]</a></sup> The homicide rates derived from criminal justice data (typically recorded by police authorities) and the public health system data (recorded when the cause of death is established) may diverge substantially for some countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC201499_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC201499-15">[14]</a></sup> The two sources usually match in the Americas, Europe and Oceania, but there are large discrepancies for the three African countries reporting both sources.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014101_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014101-16">[15]</a></sup> For the 70 countries in which neither source was made available, figures were derived from <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a> statistical models.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC201499_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC201499-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Deaths resulting from an armed conflict between states are never included in the count.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014104_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014104-17">[16]</a></sup> Killings caused by a <a href="/wiki/Non-international_armed_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-international armed conflict">non-international armed conflict</a> may or may not be included, depending on the intensity of hostilities and whether it is classified as 'civil unrest' or a clash between organized armed groups.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014104_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC2014104-17">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span id="UNODC.27s_global_study"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="UNODC's_global_study">UNODC's global study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: UNODC's global study">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>All data in this section comes from the Statistics Online website of the Research and Analysis Branch of UNODC (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-UNODCnew_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNODCnew-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unodc_gsh_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unodc_gsh-19">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_region">By region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: By region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:532px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png/530px-United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png" decoding="async" width="530" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png/795px-United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png/1060px-United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_geographical_subregions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme" title="United Nations geoscheme">United Nations geoscheme</a> with region names used in table here.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <h3><span id="By_country.2C_region.2C_or_dependent_territory"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="By_country,_region,_or_dependent_territory">By country, region, or dependent territory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: By country, region, or dependent territory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:380px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:World_murder_rate_map_2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/World_murder_rate_map_2.svg/378px-World_murder_rate_map_2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="378" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/World_murder_rate_map_2.svg/567px-World_murder_rate_map_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/World_murder_rate_map_2.svg/756px-World_murder_rate_map_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1001"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:World_murder_rate_map_2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Intentional homicide rate (per 100,000) 
         <table width="100%"> 
          <tbody>
           <tr>

      <p>The regions and region names in the table are based on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme" title="United Nations geoscheme">United Nations geoscheme</a> since the table sources are <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a> (UNODC) reports.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNODC20147–8_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNODC20147–8-21">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is a total yearly <b>count</b> of homicides for each country. <b>Rates</b> are calculated per 100,000 inhabitants. </p>
      <p><b>Subregion</b> names are based on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme" title="United Nations geoscheme">United Nations geoscheme</a>. </p>
      <p><b>Row numbers</b> are static. Other columns are sortable. This allows ranking of any column. </p>
      <p><br> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Country_subdivisions">Country subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Country subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-UNODC2013-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-UNODC2013_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.unodc.org/documents/gsh/pdfs/2014_GLOBAL_HOMICIDE_BOOK_web.pdf">2013 PDF full report</a> (<i>Global Study on Homicide</i>) has a methodological annex (pages 109ff) and a statistical annex (pages 121ff). The statistical annex has detailed charts for homicide counts and rates by country with data from 2000–2012. Map 7.2 on page 112 is a world map showing the homicide count for each country or territory. Page 21 states estimated total homicides of 437,000 worldwide. Figures 1.1 and 1.2 (pages 21 and 22) have exact rates and counts by regions. Figure 1.3 on page 23 is a bar chart of homicide rates for the subregions. Figure 1.16 on page 34 shows timeline graphs by subregion.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The UNODC report has bar charts and timeline graphs of homicide rates for subregions. But the report does not list exact rate numbers. Subregion counts are not found in the report, but may be calculated by manually totaling the counts for each country in a subregion.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
